Now I understand the escaping functions. Looking at the `format_html` function at line 135-145, I can see that it uses `conditional_escape` on all arguments. And `conditional_escape` at line 120-132 checks if the object has a `__html__` method (safe), and if not, it calls `escape`.\n\nThe `escape` function at line 53-62 uses `html.escape` which properly escapes HTML special characters.\n\nNow let me look at `format_html_join` at line 148-171, which is what's used in the `flatatt` function to render attributes.\n\nLooking at the code in `format_html_join`:\n```python\ndef format_html_join(sep, format_string, args_generator):\n    return mark_safe(\n        conditional_escape(sep).join(\n            (\n                format_html(format_string, **args)\n                if isinstance(args, Mapping)\n                else format_html(format_string, *args)\n            )\n            for args in args_generator\n        )\n    )\n```\n\nThis should properly escape attribute values because `format_html` is called with the key-value pairs, which will apply `conditional_escape` to each value.\n\nWait, looking back at `flatatt` in django/forms/utils.py:\n\n```python\ndef flatatt(attrs):\n    key_value_attrs = []\n    boolean_attrs = []\n    for attr, value in attrs.items():\n        if isinstance(value, bool):\n            if value:\n                boolean_attrs.append((attr,))\n        elif value is not None:\n            key_value_attrs.append((attr, value))\n\n    return format_html_join(\"\", ' {}=\"{}\"', sorted(key_value_attrs)) + format_html_join(\n        \"\", \" {}\", sorted(boolean_attrs)\n    )\n```\n\nThe issue is that in the format string `' {}=\"{}\"'`, the `{}` placeholders are filled with the attribute name and value. The `format_html` function should escape both the key and value.\n\n\nWhen `format_html_join` processes this, it calls `format_html(' {}=\"{}\"', attr, value)` which should escape both `attr` and `value` using `conditional_escape`. But I need to understand what the actual bug is—the report mentions that certain attribute values aren't properly escaped when they contain special characters like quotes or ampersands, causing {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01GtM7Ten14tN52PvCgA3PLa","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Aha! Here's the problem! In the `attrs.html` template at line 1:\n\n```html\n{% for name, value in widget.attrs.items %}{% if value is not False %} {{ name }}{% if value is not True %}=\"{{ value|stringformat:'s' }}\"{% endif %}{% endif %}{% endfor %}\n```\n\nThe issue is that when the value is output with `{{ value|stringformat:'s' }}`, it's using the stringformat filter with the 's' format specifier. In Django templates, by default, if a value is not marked as safe, Django applies auto-escaping. However, the issue might be that the `stringformat` filter is not properly escaping the value, or that the value is already being processed without escaping.\n\nActually, let me think about this more carefully. In modern Django templates with autoescape on (which is the default), `{{ value }}` should automatically escape HTML entities like `\"` to `&quot;`.   The decorated function will map any positional arguments after the ``*`` to\n   105→    the corresponding keyword arguments and issue a deprecation warning.\n   106→\n   107→    The decorator takes two arguments: a RemovedInDjangoXXWarning warning\n   108→    category and a list of parameter names that have been changed from\n   109→    positional-or-keyword to keyword-only, in their original To apply to a class constructor,\n   112→    decorate its __init__() method. To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n   113→    use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n   114→\n   115→    Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n   116→\n   117→        def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n   118→            ...\n   119→\n   120→    to::\n   121→\n   122→        @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n   123→        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n   124→            ...\n   125→\n   126→    After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n   127→\n   128→        def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n   129→            ...\n   130→\n   131→    Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n   132→    parameters or change the remaining ones. This change will\n   144→    work without breaking existing code::\n   145→\n   146→        @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n   147→        def some_func(request, *, new_param=None, option2=True, option1):\n   148→            ...\n   149→\n   150→    The @deprecate_posargs decorator adds a small amount of overhead. In most\n   151→    cases it won't be significant, but use with care in performance-critical\n   152→    code paths.\n   153→    \"\"\"\n   154→\n   155→    def decorator(func):\n   156→        if isinstance(func, type):\n   157→            raise TypeError(\n   158→                \"@deprecate_posargs cannot be applied to a class. In the warning, show \"ClassName()\" instead of \"__init__()\".\n   199→            # The class isn't defined yet, but its name is in __qualname__.\n   200→            # Some examples of __qualname__:\n   201→            # - ClassName.__init__\n   202→            # - Nested.ClassName.__init__\n   203→            # - MyTests.test_case.<locals>.ClassName.__init__\n   204→            local_name = func.__qualname__.rsplit(\"<locals>.\", 1)[-1]\n   205→            class_name = local_name.replace(\".__init__\", \"\")\n   206→            func_name = class_name\n   207→\n   208→        def remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs):\n   209→            \"\"\"\n   210→            Move deprecated positional args to kwargs and issue a warning.\n   211→            Return updated (args, kwargs).\n   212→            \"\"\"\n   213→            if (num_positional_args := len(args)) > max_positional_args:\n   214→                raise TypeError(\n   215→                    f\"{func_name}() takes at most {max_positional_args} positional \"\n   216→                    f\"argument(s) (including {num_remappable_args} deprecated) but \"\n   217→                    f\"{num_positional_args} were given.\"\n   218→                )\n   219→\n   220→            # Report duplicate names in the original parameter order.\n   228→                conflicts_str = \", \".join(\n   229→                    f\"'{name}'\" for name in remapped_names if name in conflicts\n   230→                )\n   231→                raise TypeError(\n   232→                    f\"{func_name}() got both deprecated positional and keyword \"\n   233→                    f\"argument values for {conflicts_str}.\"\n   234→                )\n   235→\n   236→            # (Apply it \"\n                \"to the __init__ method.)\"\n            )\n        if isinstance(func, classmethod):\n            raise TypeError(\"Apply @classmethod before @deprecate_posargs.\")\n        if isinstance(func, staticmethod):\n            raise TypeError(\"Apply @staticmethod before @deprecate_posargs.\")\n\n        params = inspect.signature(func).parameters\n        num_by_kind = Counter(param.kind for param in params.values())\n\n        if num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.VAR_POSITIONAL] > 0:\n            raise TypeError(\n                \"@deprecate_posargs() cannot be used with variable positional `*args`.\"\n            )\n\n        num_positional_params = (\n            num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.POSITIONAL_ONLY]\n            + num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.POSITIONAL_OR_KEYWORD]\n        )\n        num_keyword_only_params = num_by_kind[inspect.Parameter.KEYWORD_ONLY]\n        if num_keyword_only_params < 1:\n            raise TypeError(\n                \"@deprecate_posargs() requires at least one keyword-only parameter \"\n                \"(after a `*` entry in the parameters list).\"\n            )\n        if any(\n            name not in params or params[name].kind != inspect.Parameter.KEYWORD_ONLY\n            for name in remappable_names\n        ):\n            raise TypeError(\n                \"@deprecate_posargs() requires all remappable_names to be \"\n                \"keyword-only parameters.\"\n            )\n\n        num_remappable_args = len(remappable_names)\n        max_positional_args = num_positional_params + num_remappable_args\n\n        func_name = func.__name__\n        if func_name == \"__init__\":\n            # In the warning, show \"ClassName()\" instead of \"__init__()\".\n            # The class isn't defined yet, but its name is in __qualname__.\n            # Some examples of __qualname__:\n            # - ClassName.__init__\n            # - Nested.ClassName.__init__\n            # - MyTests.test_case.<locals>.ClassName.__init__\n            local_name = func.__qualname__.rsplit(\"<locals>.\", 1)[-1]\n            class_name = local_name.replace(\".__init__\", \"\")\n            func_name = class_name\n\n        def remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs):\n            \"\"\"\n            Move deprecated positional args to kwargs and issue a warning.\n            Return updated (args, kwargs).\n            \"\"\"\n            if (num_positional_args := len(args)) > max_positional_args:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    f\"{func_name}() takes at most {max_positional_args} positional \"\n                    f\"argument(s) (including {num_remappable_args} deprecated) but \"\n                    f\"{num_positional_args} were given.\"\n                )\n\n            # Identify which of the _potentially remappable_ params are\n            # actually _being remapped_ in this particular call.\n            remapped_names = remappable_names[\n                : num_positional_args - num_positional_params\n            ]\n            conflicts = set(remapped_names) & set(kwargs)\n            if conflicts:\n                # Report duplicate names in the original parameter order.\n                conflicts_str = \", \".join(\n                    f\"'{name}'\" for name in remapped_names if name in conflicts\n                )\n                raise TypeError(\n                    f\"{func_name}() got both deprecated positional and keyword \"\n                    f\"argument values for {conflicts_str}.\"\n                )\n\n            # Do the remapping.\n            remapped_kwargs = dict(\n                zip(remapped_names, args[num_positional_params:], strict=True)\n            )\n            remaining_args = args[:num_positional_params]\n            updated_kwargs = kwargs | remapped_kwargs\n\n            # Issue the deprecation warning.\n            remapped_names_str = \", \".join(f\"'{name}'\" for name in remapped_names)\n            warnings.warn(\n                f\"Passing positional argument(s) {remapped_names_str} to {func_name}() \"\n                \"is deprecated. Use keyword arguments instead.\",\n                deprecation_warning,\n                skip_file_prefixes=django_file_prefixes(),\n            )\n\n            return remaining_args, updated_kwargs\n\n        if iscoroutinefunction(func):\n\n            @functools.wraps(func)\n            async def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):\n                if len(args) > num_positional_params:\n                    args, kwargs = remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs)\n                return await func(*args, **kwargs)\n\n        else:\n\n            @functools.wraps(func)\n            def wrapper(*args, **kwargs):\n                if len(args) > num_positional_params:\n                    args, kwargs = remap_deprecated_args(args, kwargs)\n                return func(*args, **kwargs)\n\n        return wrapper\n\n    return decorator\n\n\nclass MiddlewareMixin:\n    sync_capable = True\n    async_capable = True\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        if get_response is None:\n            raise ValueError(\"get_response must be provided.\")\n        self.get_response = get_response\n        # If get_response is a coroutine function, turns us into async mode so\n        # a thread is not consumed during a whole request.\n        self.async_mode = iscoroutinefunction(self.get_response)\n        if self.async_mode:\n            # Mark the class as async-capable, but do the actual switch inside\n            # __call__ to avoid swapping out dunder methods.\n            markcoroutinefunction(self)\n        super().__init__()\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return \"<%s get_response=%s>\" % (\n            self.__class__.__qualname__,\n            getattr(\n                self.get_response,\n                \"__qualname__\",\n                self.get_response.__class__.__name__,\n            ),\n        )\n\n    def __call__(self, request):\n        # Exit out to async mode, if needed\n        if self.async_mode:\n            return self.__acall__(request)\n        response = None\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_request\"):\n            response = self.process_request(request)\n        response = response or self.get_response(request)\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_response\"):\n            response = self.process_response(request, response)\n        return response\n\n    async def __acall__(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Async version of __call__ that is swapped in when an async request\n        is running.\n        \"\"\"\n        response = None\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_request\"):\n            response = await sync_to_async(\n                self.process_request,\n                thread_sensitive=True,\n            )(request)\n        response = response or await self.get_response(request)\n        if hasattr(self, \"process_response\"):\n            response = await sync_to_async(\n                self.process_response,\n                thread_sensitive=True,\n            )(request, response)\n        return response\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":3,"oldLines":8,"newStart":3,"newLines":16,"lines":[" import os"," import warnings"," from collections import Counter","-from inspect import iscoroutinefunction, markcoroutinefunction","+from inspect import iscoroutinefunction"," ","+try:","+    from inspect import markcoroutinefunction","+except ImportError:","+    #
